Important News

Sixth-Third Anti-Smoking Day Commemoration Held 83

Liu Ruiheng Reports Reasons for Obstacles in Suppressing Opium

Anti-Smoking Exhibition Also Opens

The Central Opium Suppression Committee, regarding today (the 3rd) as the Sixth-Third Opium Suppression Commemoration Day, specially held a commemoration meeting this morning at the auditorium of the Ministry of Health. On this day, the national flag and the Kuomintang flag were hung at the entrance of the Ministry, and the four walls of the auditorium were covered with anti-smoking slogans. A horizontal banner read "Sixth-Third Opium Suppression Commemoration." In the center of the auditorium was a portrait of Sun Yat-sen and his last will and testament. Above it hung the Kuomintang flag, and there was also a bronze sculpture of Lin Zexu. Guests attending the meeting included Li Geng, a representative of the Central Party Headquarters, Shui Zi, a representative of the National Government, Li Danian, a representative of the Executive Yuan, and representatives from various agencies and organizations, totaling about 400 people. The meeting began at 10:00 AM, presided over by Liu Ruiheng, the chairman of the committee. The chairman led the ceremony, read Sun Yat-sen's last will and testament, and anti-drug teachings. Then, the chairman delivered an opening speech, stating that today is the Sixth-Third Opium Suppression Commemoration Day. We should feel deeply pained by the past. The Qing Dynasty believed that opium was extremely harmful and was determined to suppress it. Therefore, Lin Zexu was sent to Guangdong and Guangxi to strictly prohibit opium. More than 20,000 chests of opium were seized and burned, leading to the Opium War, the ceding of territory, and indemnities. Later, opium prohibition was relaxed, and national affairs deteriorated day by day. Although the government issued prohibition orders from time to time, opium was still not eradicated. After the establishment of the National Government, it made the greatest determination regarding opium prohibition policies and established the Opium Suppression Committee to implement opium prohibition policies. However, the reason why opium still exists today is that there are too many obstacles. One is that years of suppression wars have led to a lack of unified government orders. The second is the existence of unequal treaties, which foreigners use to transport drugs to China. The third is that opium addicts in various concessions use the concessions to sell opium. Therefore, if we want to thoroughly implement the opium prohibition policy, we must seek domestic peace and unification, abolish unequal treaties, and take back the concessions. These are the major obstacles to the opium prohibition policy. However, even before these obstacles are fundamentally removed, we must continue to work hard to complete it. Next, Li Geng, a representative of the Central Party Headquarters, delivered a speech, stating that the Qing court also issued explicit orders to ban opium, and Lin Zexu was the first person to implement opium prohibition. The reason why it was not completely eliminated was that the Qing court from top to bottom failed to lead by example and take practical action. Therefore, the so-called opium prohibition was only a formality. Although opium prohibition has been promoted for more than ten years since the establishment of the Republic of China, some warlords have even rewarded opium cultivation and sheltered the transportation of opium to make profits. The National Government has made a real determination to ban opium, so it has not been completely eliminated for a while. Therefore, there are indeed obstacles that have not been removed, as the chairman said. We hope that the government and the Party Headquarters will work together to implement the opium prohibition plan. Next, Shui Zi, a representative of the National Government, delivered a speech, stating that from the former Qing Dynasty to the present, there has been a consistent advocacy of opium prohibition policies, but the results have been very few. The reason is that there are too many obstacles. Today, we should work hard to remove obstacles to achieve thorough opium prohibition. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 AM.

In addition, the Opium Suppression Committee specially held an anti-smoking exhibition at the Jiangsu Provincial People's Education Hall on Banbian Street. It opened today (the 3rd) at 9:00 AM and will last for two weeks. The exhibits are specimens, models, and pictures related to opium suppression, totaling about several hundred kinds, which are shocking to see. In addition, the Jiangning Local Court has a large number of opium and opium paraphernalia seized in opium cases handled on weekdays. It was specially decided to burn them in the square in front of the court today (the 3rd) at 9:00 AM, totaling more than 7,000 taels of opium and more than 8,000 pieces of opium paraphernalia. The Opium Suppression Committee specially sent a member, Li Jihong, to supervise. In addition, the Opium Suppression Committee organized an opium cessation hospital branch next to the Jiangning Local Court, which also opened today (the 3rd) at 2:00 PM. There are more than 60 wards inside, and there are six doctors. The acting dean and director is Yang Jishi. It is planned to implement opium cessation in batches for the opium offenders seized by the Local Court.

Sino-Russian Conference Still Faces Many Difficulties 84

Russia's Passive Resistance to Railway Redemption Issue

Eighth Meeting May Be Postponed

Harbin Dispatch: According to the Moscow telegram obtained here, the eighth Sino-Russian conference is scheduled to be held at 4:00 PM on June 1st to discuss the issue of redeeming the Eastern Railway. It is rumored that the Russian side has proposed a redemption price of 160 million yuan. According to a telegram from Moscow, this has not been mentioned, and confirmation is still needed. However, Tu Wei, a special commissioner appointed by Mo Dehui to report to the central government, and Wang Zengsi have been transferred by the Eastern Railway Supervising Office to Moscow, urging them to quickly bring the railway redemption materials to Russia. Tu and Wang then sent a telegram saying that they are now in Beijing waiting for external documents and will go to Russia with Special Commissioner Zhang Shou Zeng on June 5th. It is heard that due to the news of the Sino-Russian conference negotiating the redemption of the railway, the old rubles accumulated for many years have been traded again, and some people are buying them in the hope that they will be used to redeem the Eastern Railway if the negotiations are successful in the future. It is also heard that a certain important person recently received a letter from a friend in Moscow detailing the situation of the Sino-Russian conference in progress. In general, after the fourth formal meeting between China and the Soviet Union, the redemption of the railway became the focus of the issue. At the fifth meeting, Karakhan made five demands, and our representative replied that there were three or several items that our side could not answer for a while. The plenipotentiary of the Soviet Union agreed to reply at the sixth meeting. After the meeting, Moscow immediately sent a telegram to the central government requesting instructions. The central government replied with a general outline and instructed the two special commissioners, Wang and Tu, to bring detailed programs when they returned to Russia. Therefore, when the sixth meeting was held on May 14th, Karakhan first asked how our side would reply to his suggestion. Moscow gave a brief reply based on the instructions of the central government and expressed deep dissatisfaction with the lack of concrete measures. Therefore, the issue of establishing a special committee to carry out valuation procedures was put on hold at the meeting on that day. When the seventh meeting was held on the 21st, Karakhan sent someone to inform him the night before that he could not attend due to illness and requested a postponement. Thus, it was postponed to the 24th for the meeting. The Russian side now has two mentalities for the meeting. One is to passively resist the railway redemption issue proposed by us by proposing a counter-proposal, so that we know the difficulty and retreat from the original proposal. Finally, we will be forced to discuss the issues of resuming transportation and commerce first. The other is to indefinitely establish a special committee to carry out valuation procedures, so that the meeting is prolonged and falls into a state of invisible stagnation. Therefore, although future meetings will still be convened on time on the surface, there will be no actual progress. The Russian side now has a wait-and-see attitude. There is a risk that the next meeting may be cancelled. According to this observation, the future of the meeting is not optimistic. Recently, the Russian government recalled consuls stationed in various parts of Northeast China and important officials of the Eastern Railway and will hold a Sino-Russian economic discussion in mid-June. Its main purpose is to develop its five-year economic plan and sell goods to China. It is implicit that the Russian side hopes to resume commerce and relations with China first. (28th)

Dispute between Beining and Kailuan Resolved 85

Kailuan Agrees to Pay 1.25 Million Yuan

Coal and Mining Contract to Be Revised by the End of the Month

Tianjin Dispatch: The dispute between the Beining Railway Bureau and the Kailuan Mining Bureau over overdue train fees and other issues has affected the coal market, causing the Chinese people to take the opportunity to call for the recovery of the Kailuan mining rights. The dispute between the railway and the mine was resolved on May 30th. The Ministry of Industry and the Hebei Industrial Department are also studying the steps to recover the mining rights. However, the dispute between the railway and the mine has lasted for more than two months. The cause and resolution of the dispute are briefly described as follows:

In March of this year, the Beining Railway discovered that the price of coal sold by Kailuan Coal Mine to the Jinpu Railway was lower than the price sold to the Beining Railway, and requested Kailuan to refund the overpaid coal price to the Beining Railway. Kailuan claimed that the Jinpu Railway was a special case and could not be used as an example. The Railway Bureau therefore demanded that Kailuan return the overdue train fees over the years and reduced the number of coal transport vehicles to show its resistance. The British general manager of Kailuan, Yang Jiali, did not want to submit to the demands of the Beining Railway and went around trying to use special forces to dispel the demands of the Beining Railway. However, the result was not achieved. At the same time, it aroused the attention of the Chinese people and there was a call for the recovery of the Kailuan mining rights. Kailuan's internal coal production could not be exported, so it wanted to stop work for two days a week, which again caused the Kailuan Miners' Union to strike. The market price of its stock also fell day by day. Therefore, Yang Jiali went to Beijing twice to visit Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and Wang's younger brother, Zhengfu, to ask them to mediate. At that time, Gao Jiyi, the director of the Beining Railway Bureau, was in Beijing with Deputy Director Zhang, and the two Wangs mediated once. Gao agreed as requested. Kailuan sent its director of general affairs, the Englishman Puaier, and Secretary-General Luo Xuchao as representatives to meet with Chen Yanjun, the chief auditor of the Beining Railway, and Chang, the director of the accounting office, at the Railway Bureau to discuss the solution. Initially, the Railway Bureau still proposed the original plan and asked Kailuan to return the overdue train fees of 1.2 million yuan and the coal price difference of 800,000 yuan since 1926. The amount that Kailuan agreed to pay was less than half of what Beining required. The reason Kailuan gave was that the overdue train fees were accumulated during the five or six years. During that time, the Railway Bureau deliberately sent the vehicles to the mining area to stop in order to avoid the army seizing the vehicles due to the war. The responsibility for this kind of overdue train cannot be borne by the mine. However, according to the old accounts of the Railway Bureau, there are only records of how many vehicles were stored in the mining area on a certain day of a certain month, and the reason cannot be proven. Therefore, the Railway Bureau agreed to reduce the overdue train fees during the war years as requested by Kailuan to show fairness. However, regarding the number, Kailuan initially agreed to pay 500,000 yuan and finally increased it to 750,000 yuan. The Railway Bureau requested 800,000 yuan for the coal price difference, which was calculated from the time the contract was revised in 1926 to the present. The difference was 0.3 yuan per ton of fine coal and 0.25 yuan per ton of lump coal. The accumulation to date should be this amount. Kailuan said that this matter has been through several directors and that the facts related to the two railway bureaus cannot be paid according to the amount proposed by Beining. It initially agreed to pay 400,000 yuan and finally increased it to 500,000 yuan. The two items totaled 1.25 million yuan, which will be allocated to the Railway Bureau on the day the contract is signed. The Railway Bureau will also provide Kailuan with as many coal transport vehicles as possible after receiving the money. The representatives of the two parties met for the last time on the 30th, and the contract has also been drafted. It is scheduled to be signed by the highest authorities of both parties on the 3rd and 4th of this month. As for the coal transport and coal use contracts signed with Beining, they are all limited to the end of June this year. At that time, they must be renegotiated. It is heard that the previously signed contract was very preferential to Kailuan. When the new contract is revised in the future, it will be treated according to the precedents of Chinese coal merchants and will no longer be given special treatment to maintain the sales market of Chinese-owned coal mines. (June 1st)

Measures to Regulate Farmers' Economy in Northeast China 86

Oversupply and Stagnant Sales of Soybeans

Order to Change to Other Grains

Jilin Dispatch: Among the special products of the Northeast, soybeans are the most important. All parties at home and abroad recognize it as the most abundant area for soybean production. However, due to the lack of knowledge of farmers and merchants and the failure to pay attention to quality, the quality has gradually declined, resulting in the elimination of the European market and the formation of an oversupply and stagnant sales situation. The official silver bank of the three northeastern provinces takes the balance of supply and demand as the principle of economy. Therefore, the quantity of production must be adjusted according to the degree of need. Otherwise, there will be a shortage or surplus. Our country's agricultural products are the best in the world, but because the balance between surplus and deficiency cannot be averaged, both rice and noodles feel lacking, and foreign imports are alarming every year. On the contrary, soybeans feel that production is surplus, resulting in delayed sales. In recent years, the price of soybeans in foreign markets has suddenly fallen, which is due to the economic depression of the world, but in fact, the excess of supply over demand has caused it. How can the farmers in the remote countryside see this? If they are allowed to continue to plant, not only will production increase day by day and sales become more stagnant, but I am afraid that the land, capital, and labor will be lost. In addition to soybeans, there are many things that can be planted in the three provinces. For example, it is suitable to grow wheat north of Changchun, and it is suitable to grow miscellaneous grains and other oil grains south of Changchun. Cotton can also be tried. In addition, there are many places where paddy fields can be opened up to grow rice. As long as we observe the suitability of the soil and the accuracy of the climate, success can be expected. If it is suitable for wheat, grow wheat. If there is more wheat, there will be no shortage of flour, and foreign flour can be prevented from being imported. If it is suitable for rice, grow rice. If there is more rice, there will be more rice, and foreign rice will not come from other sources. Other miscellaneous grains, cotton, and other things have corresponding uses and corresponding values. It is not difficult to profit by making up for the deficiency. If supply and demand can be balanced, all agricultural products will not be oversupplied and stagnated, and the farmers' economy will naturally develop. Now, the silver bank has submitted this regulatory measure to the Northeast Political Committee to order the governments of the three provinces to instruct the counties to advise farmers to plant less soybeans and change to other equivalent agricultural products in the future. On the one hand, the county government or local organizations, such as agricultural associations, will convene local gentry or people who are proficient in agricultural science and experienced farmers to jointly study and improve according to local conditions to make adjustments and increase production. The Political Committee believes that the above-mentioned sections are for the purpose of remedying agriculture. Last fall, due to the stagnant sales of soybeans, farmers and merchants suffered hardships. If they are still ignorant of the principle of supply and demand and do not think about adapting to local conditions to improve production, the future of agriculture will inevitably lead to the destruction of vitality, and the national economy and people's livelihood will suffer. It has immediately ordered the three provinces to transfer the order to the agricultural and mineral bureaus to order the counties to supervise the agricultural associations to study the planting of equivalent grains to increase income. The various bureaus in this province have followed the order and instructed their subordinate departments to comply. (28th)

Railway Inspection Group Arrives in Shenyang from Japan 87

Bao De talks about how this trip is worthwhile

Shenyang Dispatch: The railway observation group sent by the Ministry of Railways to Japan arrived in Shenyang from Dalian on the 28th. The group has a total of 18 people and is jointly organized by the Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo, Longhai, Jiaoji, Beining, Jinpu six lines and the Ministry of Railways. The list is as follows: Head of the group: Cheng Zhigang, Director of Documents: Sun Xuexiu, Director of General Affairs: Zhu Bi, Members: Zhong Dan and his wife Liu Huaiwei, Sun Jialu, Xiong Zhengwan, Zeng Guanghe, Chen Guangyuan, Gu Qiwen, Qi Lianyao, Gu Tingyue, Che Shaoling, Luan BaoDe, Lu Tingsi, Xu Zhongwei, Su Baoshan, Sun Wenzao. They stayed in the Ling Ge Kai Ning and Liao Ning three hotels. They have been very busy visiting the machine factories of Beining, Shenhai, and South Manchuria for several days. Yesterday, the reporter met with Luan BaoDe, a member of the group, at the Ling Ge Hotel. According to him, the group stayed in Japan for more than forty days before coming to Shenyang. All major railway machine factories in Japan have been visited. The internal management equipment of the factory is planned by the Ministry of Railways, and the content of each factory is unified. Moreover, most of them have been scientific, so the efficiency is high and the cost is low. The main point of our group's visit this time is the railway machinery factory. The result is quite satisfactory and not in vain. In the future, we will adopt its strengths to reform the machine factories of each road in our country. Due to the limited time, it is decided to leave Shenyang on the 31st and follow the Beining Road to Shanhaiguan, then to Tangshan, Tianjin, and Beiping, and then transfer to Jinpu Road to Jinan, change to Jiaoji Road to Qingdao, and then return to Pukou to return to Beijing to report. (29th)

Henan Seventeenth Division Launches Suppression of Zhang Guancheng's Fierce Bandits 88

Kaifeng Dispatch: Notorious bandits Zhang Guancheng, Li Shuangcheng, Zhang Ke, Zhang Lue, Feng Gongwa, Zhang Xiaoping, etc. have about three to four hundred bandits, who are exceptionally fierce. They use villages such as Ao Tou, Xi He, Shang Yao Wan, and Shang Zhuang in the southeast of Ziyou County as their nests, and harass and plunder everywhere. The bandits broke through and looted Yiyang County last year, taking away more than 300 women. Other villages bordering the three counties of Ziyou, Yiyang, and Linru, such as Jin Zhuang, Nei Bu, Du Zhuang, and Lou, have suffered as much as Yiyang County. Shi Keqin's brigade of the Seventy-fifth Division began to suppress the bandit's nest from Linru Town on the 23rd of this month. Li Yaguang, the chief of staff of the division, specially went to Linru Town to discuss the suppression plan with Brigade Commander Shi in order to be cautious. The plan is that the bandit's nests of Ao Tou, Xi He, Shang Yao, and Shang Zhuang are horns to each other and help each other. It is difficult to attack. It is better to use the method of attacking the east and west to tire the bandits. After they are tired, use fierce artillery fire to attack the three villages of Xi He, Shang Yao, and Shang Zhuang at the same time. Then send a surprise force to attack their rear, so that the bandits cannot take care of each other. After the plan was determined, the three villages were successively broken through on the 26th. In this battle, more than 70 bandits were killed and more than 100 guns were captured. More than 50 male and female tickets were shot down. Seven officers and soldiers were killed and wounded. A small number of the remaining bandits escaped into the mountains with their families. The brigade has sent teams to intercept them. The remaining bandits trapped in Ao Tou have become turtles in a jar. Today, Brigade Commander Shi has used fierce artillery fire to bombard the village and has also erected many ladders in preparation for climbing the bandit's nest. The breakthrough of the bandit's nest should be in the next day or two.

Relaxing of City Streets Submitted to the Ministry for Approval: The streets in the city are narrow. Since the opening of the road, pedestrians have felt the hardship of having to give way. Zhong Tai, the chief of the first district, once proposed to widen the streets, and the district affairs meeting decided to submit it to the county government for approval so that a committee could be organized to actively carry it out. It is now learned that the county government has handed it over to the Construction Bureau for review, and the Construction Bureau has submitted another plan. After the 109th meeting of the county government, the plan proposed by the First District Office was temporarily shelved, and the plan of the Construction Bureau was submitted to the Ministry for approval. It is heard that this great project is related to the prosperity of the city and its commerce. The Construction Bureau will prepare to carry it out as soon as it receives the approval from the Ministry to comfort those who look forward to it.

Suzhou 91

Divorce Case of Hu Zhiqin Ended in Appeal and Settlement: Hu Zhiqin, a teacher at the French Concession of Shanghai, is 25 years old. When he was 16 years old, Hu worked as an accountant in a cloth shop and met Yang Shuzhen, a woman from Changzhou (21 years old this year) who lived next to the shop. They soon fell in love and rented a house at Nine Mu Di inside Xiao Bei Men. Hu had many friends who often visited his house, and Hu suspected that his friend Wang Jingfei was having an affair with Yang Shuzhen. Until the spring of last year, Hu and Yang quarreled and broke up and signed a divorce contract. Afterwards, Hu suddenly asked Yang Shuzhen's family for compensation for losses. Yang Shuzhen then hired lawyer Li Yuan to file a lawsuit with the Shanghai Local Court to request the dissolution of the marriage contract. On December 30th, the plaintiff's lawsuit was rejected. Yang Shuzhen appealed to the High Court. Yesterday (the 3rd), Judge Lu Wenlan of the Second Civil Division of the High Court held a trial and persuaded them to settle. Yang Shuzhen's mother and daughter did not want to compensate Hu Zhiqin because Yang Shuzhen had been raped by Hu Zhiqin for two years. Hu Zhiqin claimed that both parties agreed to get engaged and live together. They accused me of smoking opium and not doing my job, but I also worked as a contributor to the Robin Hood tabloid in Shanghai. I don't smoke opium now. As for their request for termination of the contract, the appellant must compensate for the losses of the previous engagement of 700 yuan, and he and Wang Jingfei had a physical relationship. Judge Lu persuaded them to settle again, and Yang's mother and daughter also wanted Hu to compensate for the damage to their reputation. As a result, Judge Lu persuaded Yang Shuzhen to pay Hu Zhiqin 170 yuan to settle. Judge Lu drafted the settlement contract and adjourned the court.

Wuxi 92

The Wuxi Gendarmerie is Preparing to Depart: The Wuxi Gendarmerie Fourth Regiment has been ordered to leave Suzhou and go to Wuxi to perform road protection duties since February 16th of this year, and it has been four months. They have paid great attention to the defense aspect. The acting regiment commander, Ying Huaizong, received a telegram from Gu Zhenglun, the commander of the Capital Garrison, the other day, ordering the entire regiment to prepare to depart and concentrate in Zhenjiang to wait for further orders. After receiving the order, the acting regimental commander has prepared everything and will depart to Zhenjiang as soon as the order arrives to concentrate in one place to await orders to depart. The defense duties left behind will be taken over by a team sent by the First Regiment stationed in Suzhou.

The Silkworm Cocoon Trade in the Four Townships is Opening in Order: The standard opening date for the silkworm cocoon trade in the four townships has been decided by the Silk Cocoon Industry Association to be the 4th of this month. However, due to the different climates in each township, the eastern route has already opened the other day. It is estimated that there are four families in Dongting Town, including Dongchang Yu, Pinghe, Yuchang, and Fuyuan, with a cocoon price of 50 yuan per tan. The western route, including Qianzhou and Yuqi, is scheduled to open today. At present, various silk factories have dispatched temporary staff to report to the Cocoon Industry Association yesterday morning. Those who have reported opening include Erfang, Xia Yuan, Zhang She, Henghe, and Baxi Bridge Guo Xiechang, etc., totaling forty-five families. The total before and after is 117 families, exceeding one-third of the cocoon trade in the county.

Tea Tax to Be Implemented: The original tea stand tax in the county, which is 7 cents per tea stand per month, subsidizes the police expenses and is collected by the Municipal Fund Production Committee. Qian Zhongliang, the chief of the first district, proposed to collect a copper coin per pot of tea from tea guests to be used as autonomous funding because the autonomous funding of various townships was not available. Teahouse merchants expressed their opposition after hearing this, saying that one industry cannot be taxed twice. It is now heard that the tea stand tax can be stopped, and the tea guest tax can be implemented. However, the opinions of the tea merchants are still not consistent. The Qingxiang Committee Re-investigates Household Registration: The Provincial Qingxiang General Bureau recently appointed Ni Weiqing, etc. to go to Jiangyin, Jingjiang, Taicang, Jiading, Wuxian, and Wuxi to investigate Qingxiang affairs. Commissioner Ni came to Wuxi the other day and went to the county government to meet with County Magistrate Pan to investigate Qingxiang work. Then, County Magistrate Pan appointed Shen Zao, the chief of the second section, to accompany him to the Qingxiang First Sub-bureau (i.e., the first district) for inspection. After that, he set off to re-investigate the household registration. Commissioner Ni went to the second, fourth, tenth, and seventeenth districts for inspection in recent days. According to Commissioner Ni, this time, the investigation in various counties believes that the names of the local defense regiments are different and they are all nominal and not real. They should be reorganized and renamed in accordance with the law in order to maintain the locality. The registration of ships, household registration investigation, joint insurance measures, and firearm inspection must also be handled separately item by item.

Changshu 93

The Yongyu Qianzhuang (Money Shop) Collapses: In the autumn of last year, Gu Guang from Shanghai, along with Yang Peifu and Qin Kanru and others from this town, organized a money shop inside the Guangtai Tin Foil Shop in the North Market of the city, naming it Yongyu. They appointed Qin Kanru as the general manager and Chen Luncai as the deputy. It opened in September but had not joined the Qianye Gonghui (Money Industry Association). It is said that the shop only had a capital of twenty to thirty thousand yuan, but the account books and used promissory notes reached seventeen thousand yuan. From the very beginning, the shop issued many of its own promissory notes, which were discounted everywhere to make up for the turnover. This was a dangerous move of virtual capital and actual profit. At the end of last month, the shop failed to redeem its own promissory notes for foreign currency because it was short two thousand five hundred yuan, leading to its collapse. Chen Luncai and others, seeing that they could not manage, left Changshu first. General Manager Qin Kanru, seeing the crowds of people holding notes for redemption, borrowed the excuse of going out to plan and also fled. Soon, Lawyer Chen prepared a notice to liquidate. According to those familiar with the financial world, the shop has a book loss of sixteen thousand yuan, with an actual loss of only fifteen thousand five hundred yuan. However, the shop has issued many promissory notes, and peers are concerned about the relationship between the shop's notes and themselves. To maintain their own credit, it is said that they will issue a redemption of the shop's notes, otherwise future note issuances will definitely be questioned. As for deposits and debts, they will be discounted in the future, but all large and small businesses here are affected.

The Robbery Case in the Fifth District is Solved: Xu Zhang's family in Xujia Village near Cuiqiao in the Fifth District of Wu County was robbed previously. The first branch of the tenth public security bureau under its jurisdiction captured two robbers, Qian Gensheng and Zhong Longbao, and brought them to the county for interrogation. Two days later, Inspector Zhu Sen also arrested the bandit Sun Fengfeng, involved in the case, in Sunjia Village. That night, he sent the police to escort them to the city and handed them over to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Fire in Shengze Kills Four: The Rongxing Inn in Xinkai Lane, Shengze Town, under the county, caught fire in the firewood room at one o'clock the previous morning, which spread to the Sanxin Hotel. After the Longshe (Fire Brigade) in each section made every effort to rescue, it did not spread to other houses. However, the owner of the Rongxing Inn, Yan Bingyong, and his two sons and one daughter were all burned to death, which is truly tragic.

Nantong 96

The Wounded Soldiers' Factory is Temporarily Difficult to Relocate: After Zhuang Mingyuan, the director of the Eleventh Division's Wounded Soldiers' Factory, explained the misunderstanding to the local authorities, the factory started work first. Commander Luo Zhuoying telegraphed the county government and various groups from Nanchang, stating that the division's wounded soldiers' factory was temporarily borrowing the poverty-stricken workers' workplace to start operations in order to show consideration for the revolutionary soldiers. He hoped that the local groups would deeply understand this purpose and assist them. He further stated that the soldiers of the headquarters would strictly abide by discipline and guaranteed that nothing would happen. He also hoped that local people would uphold the principle of kinship and love the soldiers.

Kunshan 97

The Police Team Captures Bandits: Recently, robbery cases have occurred frequently in the Four Zou area, and there have been few successes in solving them, so bandits have become fearless. A few days ago, the Cuiyuan Oil Shop outside the East and West Gates was robbed by bandits, losing over one thousand yuan in cash and banknotes. Magistrate Gong was furious upon hearing this and immediately ordered Wu Shaokang, the head of the detective team, to solve the case within five days. Two days later, Luo Qixiang, the police chief, learned that the bandits were hiding in Wuxi and immediately ordered Officer Kong of the water police to lead a team of officers to capture them as the opportunity arose. After Kong arrived in Wuxi, he saw that the bandits had already purchased train tickets and boarded a train to Shanghai. He waited on either side of them. Near Kunshan Station, he gave a command and stepped forward to capture them, arresting Yang Xiude, Xiao Guo, Ji Ruchai, and Meng Yuqing. They were immediately escorted to the team headquarters. The bandit leader is still in Wuxi and is being arrested. It is estimated that they will be escorted to Kunshan this afternoon and dealt with according to law.

Robbery and Injury in Yongan Town: Yongan Town, within the jurisdiction of the Eighth Public Security Bureau, was visited yesterday by four bandit ships speaking in the dialect of Yanfu. More than twenty bandits, carrying a dozen or so guns, landed and robbed several shops, injuring two shop assistants. They then took the loot and left. The Ministry of Education Announces the Revised Regulations on School Holidays 100

Effective from August 1st of this year.

Yesterday (2nd), the Ministry of Education issued a decree announcing the revised Regulations on the School Year, Semesters, and Holiday Dates, consisting of eleven articles, which differ greatly from the old holiday regulations. They are recorded as follows:

Article 1: The school year for all levels of schools starts on August 1st of each year and ends on July 31st of the following year.

Article 2: A school year is divided into two semesters: the first semester runs from August 1st to January 31st of the following year, and the second semester runs from February 1st to July 31st.

Article 3: In each semester, the number of school days, excluding the dates of Type A holidays in Article 4, shall be determined according to the following regulations: Universities and colleges: 136 days in the first semester, 135 days in the second semester (136 days in leap years); Secondary schools: 143 days in the first semester, 141 days in the second semester (143 days in leap years); Elementary schools: 146 days in the first semester, 145 days in the second semester (146 days in leap years).

Article 4: The annual holiday dates for all levels of schools shall be determined according to the following regulations: Type A Holidays: (1) Summer Vacation: Universities and colleges: limited to 70 days (from June 23rd to August 31st); Secondary schools: limited to 56 days (from June 30th to August 24th); Elementary schools: limited to 50 days (from July 3rd to August 21st); (2) New Year's Holiday: All schools shall uniformly set it as three days (from January 1st to January 3rd); (3) Winter Vacation: All levels of schools shall uniformly set it as fourteen days (from January 18th to January 31st); (4) Spring Vacation: All levels of schools shall uniformly set it as seven days (from April 1st to April 7th); Type B Commemorative Holidays: (1) Confucius' Birthday Memorial Day (August 27th in the Gregorian calendar); (2) National Day Memorial Day (October 10th in the Gregorian calendar); (3) Sun Yat-sen's Birthday Memorial Day (November 12th in the Gregorian calendar);

(4) Founding of the Republic of China Memorial Day (January 1st in the Gregorian calendar); (5) Sun Yat-sen's Death Memorial Day (March 12th in the Gregorian calendar); (6) Revolutionary Martyrs' Memorial Day (March 29th in the Gregorian calendar); (7) Revolutionary Government Memorial Day (May 5th in the Gregorian calendar); (8) National Revolutionary Army Oath-Taking Memorial Day (July 9th in the Gregorian calendar). All levels of schools shall have a one-day holiday on each of the commemorative days listed on the right and shall hold a memorial ceremony and speech on that day.

Article 5: Special local commemorative days that require a holiday must be determined by the Provincial Education Department or the Municipal Education Bureau of municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan and reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 6: The number of school anniversary holidays for each level of school shall not exceed two days per year.

Article 7: Except for Sundays and various holiday dates in Articles 4, 5, and 6, no holidays may be taken arbitrarily. Various gatherings shall be held on Sundays.

Article 8: The school calendar for universities and colleges shall be prepared by each school based on these regulations and the Concise List of Revolutionary Memorial Days, the Brief History of Revolutionary Memorial Days, and the Key Points of Propaganda passed by the First Standing Committee of the Central Committee, two months before the start of the school year, and reported directly or forwarded to the Ministry of Education for approval. The school calendar for secondary and elementary schools shall be prepared and promulgated by the Provincial Education Department or the Municipal Education Bureau of municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan based on these regulations and the Concise List of Revolutionary Memorial Days, the Brief History of Revolutionary Memorial Days, and the Key Points of Propaganda passed by the Hundredth Standing Committee of the Central Committee, two months before the start of the school year, and reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

Secondary and elementary schools affiliated with national or private universities and colleges, and secondary and elementary schools established by various agencies of the National Government in various provinces or municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan, shall follow the school calendar prepared and promulgated by the local Education Department or Education Bureau. The same applies to secondary and elementary schools affiliated with provincial universities and colleges in the municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan.

Article 9: The start and end dates of the summer vacation for rural elementary schools with special circumstances may be adjusted (such as advancing or delaying) according to the local agricultural conditions, and the vacation may be divided into several sections for intermittent holidays (such as separate farming holidays, wheat holidays, autumn harvest holidays, etc.) to reduce the number of summer vacation days. However, the total number of holiday days shall not exceed the limit of 50 days and must be approved by the Provincial Education Department or the Municipal Education Bureau of municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan.

Article 10: The start and end dates of winter and summer vacations in provinces and cities with severe cold and heat may be changed according to local conditions, but the total number of holiday days shall not exceed the regulations in items (1) and (3) of Article 4, and must be reported to the Ministry of Education by the Provincial Education Department or the Municipal Education Bureau of municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan for approval.

Article 11: These regulations shall come into effect on August 1, 1931.

Local News

The Municipal Party Headquarters Announces Measures for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Teachers 101

The Measures for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers and the Detailed Rules of Procedure for the Meetings of the Committee for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers in Shanghai Municipality were previously drafted by the Municipal Training Department and submitted to the Municipal Executive Committee for record. The Municipal Executive Committee has now approved the record with Directive No. 463. The review measures are recorded below, and it is announced that the review committee is scheduled to begin the review on the 10th of this month.

Measures for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers in Shanghai Municipality

(1) The matter of reviewing the qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers shall be decided by the committee and held in stages, but must be held at least once a year. (2) The review period for each stage shall not exceed three months. (3) All documents and clerical work during the review period shall be handled by the Party Ideology Education Section of the Municipal Training Department. (4) The review work shall be assigned by the Standing Committee members to committee members. (5) All review matters must be approved by the committee meeting. (6) Temporary meetings may be held when necessary outside the review period. (7) The Party Ideology Teachers who pass the review shall be reported by the committee to the Municipal Executive Committee for approval and issuance of certificates, and the names of qualified personnel shall be announced. (8) These measures shall be implemented after being approved by the committee and recorded by the Municipal Executive Committee.

The Upcoming International Games 103

Preparations are Complete

This year's Shanghai International Games will be held this Saturday and Sunday. A total of nine countries are participating, with more than 250 athletes, both men and women. All are elites from various countries in Shanghai, and it is a grand event of the moment. In recent days, the authorities have spared no effort in compiling and printing the order of events, arranging the venue, and so on.

Fu Shengji Reports on the Tournament: Athletes from nine countries in Europe, America, and Asia are gathered together. It is expected that a large number of spectators will be present at the time. Leyu defeated Benliu by a score of 32 to 18 in the final last night.

The Jingwu Team Gave Up the Right to the Final in a Gesture of Modesty.

The Jingwu Athletic Association, composed of 24 elite troops and a hundred great generals, initiated the Jingwu Cup after more than a month of competition, with strengths and weaknesses already determined and high and low scores divided. Last night was the final scene, and as a result, Benliu lost to Leyu by a score of 32 to 18, and Leyu won the championship.

Benliu Occupies the Top Spot 105

Leyu's Efforts Fall Short 106

In the past, its achievements were better than Benliu, and the talent was also evenly matched. However, in last night's battle, it was difficult to see fluency in attack and defense. In the first half, it was able to deal with the situation, losing by only 13 to 14. In the second half, it was greatly disappointed and suffered an irreversible defeat. It can truly be said that its efforts fell short.

Jingwu's Modesty is Admirable 107

The Jingwu Team is also one of the three groups (Wuzi Group) and the champion of the group. The ball skills and talent are said to be the best of the time, and the call for winning the championship is the highest. However, as the host, it did not want to occupy the top spot, so it announced its abandonment of the final to show great fairness and impartiality. This kind of modesty is rare in the sports world. The team roster is as follows: Captain Guo Zhihong, Secretary Chen Chihua, and members Hu Keli, Chen Jiasheng, Jian Shiyong, Yan Tinghui, Mai Zihuai, Ren Zhongling, Shen Bingcong, and Chen Runsheng.

Jiangnan University Men's and Women's Volleyball Tournament: Fudan and Jinan are Champions 108

Fudan defeated Jinan 3-0 to win the men's championship.

Jinan defeated Jiaotong 3-2 to win the women's championship.

The Jiangnan University Volleyball Championship was held in two groups, A and B. As a result, Fudan and Jinan won the top spots in the two groups, and the women's championship was won by Jinan and Jiaotong. At 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the four teams competed in the men's and women's championship finals at the China Athletic Field. The women's group competed first, with Jinan defeating Jiaotong 3-2 to win the championship. In the men's group, Fudan defeated Jinan 3-0 to maintain its third consecutive year of victory.

Jinan Wins the Women's Championship 109

The Jinan women's team and the Jiaotong women's team first competed in the women's championship final. After fierce competition between the two teams, Jinan reversed the defeat and won 3-2 against Jiaotong to win the championship.

All Thanks to Luck: The strength of the Jinan and Jiaotong teams is similar, with little difference between the top and bottom. Therefore, yesterday's victory or defeat was determined by luck. The closeness of the scores is evident. Jinan won the first game, and Jiaotong won two games in a row, taking a 2-1 lead. Jinan then won another game to tie the score at 2-2. The intensity and tension of the final five minutes of the fifth game were indescribable. After 18-18, the score became 20-20 again. When Jiaotong added a point to make the score 21-20, the Jiaotong team thought they had won and cheered loudly, but the referee announced a dead ball and ordered a re-serve. With luck on their side, Jinan scored consecutive points and won the championship.

Unpredictable Situation: A brief description of the five games: Jiaotong attacked first, with Wu Shiying serving and scoring two consecutive points. In the first instance, Jinan's Huang Rushuang returned the ball too heavily and it flew out of bounds, and Jiaotong gained a point. Later, Jinan's Deng Zhijun also scored two points. After the score was 2-2, the two sides killed each other, and Zhang Junsun scored six consecutive points with accuracy and strength, giving Jiaotong an 11-6 lead in the first half. Unfortunately, they made a lot of mistakes after that, and the first game ended in defeat with a score of 17-21. Such is the unpredictability of victory and defeat. In the second game, Jiaotong played carefully and prudently, and saw a turnaround. In the first half, they won a great victory by a score of 11-4. Jinan also stepped up their efforts and caught up, tying the score several times. Jiaotong finally won 21-19, each winning one game. Continuing to play carefully, Jiaotong won the third game and took a 2-1 lead. With their confidence relaxed, they thought they could relax a little, so mistakes gradually appeared, and they lost two games in a row. Jinan then rose sharply and won the championship. This is another unpredictable change in victory and defeat.

Talent of the Two Teams: In one sentence, Jinan's victory was due to the average talent, strong physical strength, and the fact that both passing and spiking reached a good level, making them extremely promising material. Jiaotong, on the other hand, was uneven, with the good being too good and the weak being too weak. People like Tao Chun, Zhang Junsun, Hou Yufen, and Wu Shu were all veterans of the Sanjingzhi. Unfortunately, there were one or two who were too weak, which often led to positional conflicts. It is said that Jiaotong has a total of 18 female students, and this team is already a sight to behold.

Words of Wisdom 117

— Yi Mei

He who carries a watch may not be able to keep time; he who wears a foreign pen on his lapel may not be fluent in foreign languages.

Things can be held back in value to wait for a good price, but virtue should not be devalued for the sake of selling.

The discarded manuscript paper of a scholar is no different from the tattered clothes patched together by a poor man.

Having a thatched cottage to store books and a piece of land to plant bamboo is enough for my whole life.

Knowing when to act is the way to be a hero; digesting and transforming the past is the way to be a sage.

Better to be a capable laborer than a useless idler.

The most worrying thing is having a name without substance, not worrying about having substance without a name.

Both warmth and cold can be endured, but the most difficult to bear are sudden heat and sudden cold.

The wilderness is completely ancient, but even planting one or two telephone poles seems particularly glaring.

The demons of modernity do not know how much disaster they cause to young people.

Those who admire the rich are not rich; those who are content with poverty are not poor.

Prepare for famine in advance, so that there is no need to provide relief afterwards.

The virtue of a person is like the color of the moon and the fragrance of a flower.

When dealing with the world, one should have a cool head and a passionate heart.

I would rather live in a place of clear mountains and waters than be drunk in the noisy city.

He who seeks himself is honored; he who seeks others is humiliated.

Ancient sages competed in drinking at the wine table; modern people dance and squander in the pavilion.

Some use air travel to forge a hundred years of friendship, and others inscribe gifts with the words "flying birds together," which can be said to be elegant and unique.

Anecdotes of Feng Junmu 118

— Jie Lu

Mr. Feng, whose given name was , was a native of Cixi, Zhejiang. He lost his father in his youth and was known for his filial piety towards his mother. His mother, née Yu, was from a prominent family in the town and educated her son with utmost strictness. She burned the midnight oil, personally tutoring him for several years, and as a result, he achieved great academic success. In a certain year during the Guangxu reign of the late Qing dynasty, he was recommended as a tribute student and became very close friends with Ying Qizhi, who was from the same town. Ying was also a man of extraordinary talent and was considered his equal at the time. At that time, the Qing government was corrupt and the country was in decline. Mr. Feng was deeply worried about this, so he and like-minded people in the town established Cihu Middle School, Zhengshi Elementary School, and Dongcheng Girls' School, pioneering the educational atmosphere in Zhejiang. At that time, Zhejiang students studying in Japan published the "Zhejiang Tide" to awaken the demoralized people. Mr. Feng wrote several poems and sent them to the magazine, expressing profound and subtle sentiments. Liang Qichao of Xinhui saw them and exclaimed in amazement, "This young man is not to be taken lightly!" He immediately published them in the "Xinmin congbao" which he edited. Later, when Chen Tianying founded the "Tiantuo bao" in Shanghai, he hired Mr. Feng to manage the fiction section. His essays, along with those of Hong Foshi and Dai Jitao in the newspaper, were known as the "Three Talents of Tiantuo." A few years ago, Mr. Qin Runqing founded the Xiuneng Study Society in Shanghai and hired Mr. Feng as the director of the Arts Department. He devoted himself wholeheartedly to planning and achieved remarkable results. Mr. Feng had a simple and unadorned disposition and did not enjoy seeking official positions. He associated with many virtuous gentlemen in Shanghai, often discussing poetry and literature, and his home was always full of guests. He also loved to encourage younger generations. If anyone was even slightly talented, he would always praise them endlessly. He was especially concerned about the sons of his old friends, doing his best to promote and support them. His friend Kuang Huifeng of Lingui was a lyricist who was not good at officialdom, and lived a simple life, leaving nothing behind after his death. Mr. Feng not only cared for his son but also instructed his second son to marry Kuang’s daughter. A friend from the same town, Wei Gaixiang, had a son who was quite intelligent. After Wei died, Mr. Feng immediately married his daughter to Wei's son. Mr. Feng's way of handling his children's marriages is worthy of emulation. I have a cousin, Shufei, who is Mr. Feng's nephew. My late uncle passed away early, and Mr. Feng treated Shufei as his own son. Their fraternal affection was especially sincere and deep. My family was originally poor, but now Shufei is able to support himself. It can be said that my late uncle has descendants thanks entirely to Mr. Feng's efforts. When I was young, I was still aware of the need to strive, and Mr. Feng loved me very much. He once wrote to my father, urging me to abandon commerce and pursue education. My family had a traditional business, and my father did not agree. After I had been a merchant for only half a month, I received a letter from Mr. Feng and returned home. Alas, my father passed away last winter, and now Mr. Feng has also passed away. As I write this, I cannot continue. Alas! (Reverberating Sigh)

A Record of Appreciating Flowers in the Rain at Little Guanyuan Garden 119

— Ting Bing Sheng

Jiangwan is very close to Shanghai. Mr. Yang Shouren, the director of Little Guanyuan Garden, wanted to appreciate peonies, so we drove there together. Those who went with me were Shen Guoliang, the chairman of the Dongjiadu Fire Prevention Association, as well as Zhu Pinggu, Section Chief Huang Guangdou of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and literary friends Shen Yongqing and Zhang Ruogu. That day, the sky was cloudy and there was a hint of rain. Everyone brought raincoats and hunting hats, and our joyful mood was not diminished at all. When we arrived at the garden gate, Director Yang was already there to greet us on the side of the road. We got out of the car and greeted each other with joy, and then he led us to sit in the thatched hall. The four walls were painted silver-gray, and the light gleamed like shattered glass. In the middle, there was a platform on which were placed a dozen or so pots of roses and peonies. The vermillion faces and verdant vines, the drunken pink and charming reds, reflected and enhanced each other, making them extremely beautiful. We sat in order and sipped tea in front of the flowers. It seemed as if a faint fragrance flew over the water and filled our noses, allowing us to forget the world. Suddenly, the rain started, falling in continuous strands. All we could see were blurry green shadows, and we couldn't distinguish the branches and leaves. The rain subsided slightly, and the accumulated mist gradually dissipated. The air became fresher and the scenery became even greener. A patch of new green was like jade or emerald brocade. The mud on the branches and leaves seemed to have been washed clean. The multicolored flowers shimmered among the dense greens, like the smile of a young girl. It was a breathtaking sight! Then we all went to the flower garden, stepping on the soft paths and pushing aside the wet grass, walking slowly along the zigzag path, without raising any dust. The gentle coolness felt comfortable on the body. Everywhere we looked, the flowers competed for beauty. I especially loved a "Heart of Ice" rose among the monthly roses. Its color was pure white like mercury, and its petals were large and faced upwards, budding and blooming, as beautiful as a young woman in plain white standing under a white plum tree. There was also a type of "Oriole" rose, whose stamens were deep red like pearls and wine, and whose outer petals were light pink, also lovely, like a dancing girl swaying on a red carpet. There was another type of rose, whose flowers were bright red and clean, as if they would drip, covered with raindrops, looking like a drunken beauty with a plump figure and a coquettish posture. Mr. Zhu pointed to a yellow flower and showed it to me. The shape of its flower was the same as that of a morning glory, and its outer layer was light crimson, which reminded people of Xi Shi frowning. In total, there were about a thousand types of roses, half of which came from America, half from Germany, and the rest were domestic and Japanese varieties. Director Yang said that buying these seeds cost more than three thousand dollars, but only four or five out of ten were able to bloom luxuriantly and beautifully all year round. Section Chief Huang then said that flower workers were more difficult than doctors, because doctors could diagnose illnesses and inquire about the source of the patient's pain, while flower workers could only understand the flowers' proud "smiles," but the flowers could not speak. His words were very clever. Then Chairman Shen suddenly exclaimed, "I have found a rare flower!" Everyone rushed to look at it. The flower's color was a rich, purplish-red, piled with red blushes. Its edges were all wrapped with golden silk, only as long as a hair. It had never been seen before. Director Yang also praised this flower as the crown of the garden, but it only bloomed once a year and had not yet been named. The peonies in the garden included those that were as red as belts, like peonies; those that were slightly green, like green plums; those that were as slender as wisteria flowers; and those that were as vibrant as roses. The tender yellows and light purples swayed and emitted fragrance. It was a pity that I could not describe them all. Their fragrance and color were truly a regret. Soon after, we returned to the thatched hall for a banquet. As the wine flowed and our ears became heated, the gentlemen who accompanied me ordered me to write a record of it. I complied and wrote this without any understanding.

Evening Talk at Huiju's Home 120

— Zi Wei

Many famous actors who come to the South are usually overwhelmed with banquets. Due to time constraints, they often leave the table after sitting for a short while, and the hosts and guests are only able to enjoy each other's company for a brief time, which is always a pity. The organizers of the Mingxing Opera Troupe are well aware of this, so they usually invite guests to the troupe after the performance at midnight to offer a welcome dinner, not adhering to conventional customs. They sip lightly and chat late into the night, which is also a good way to cut candles and see each other's friendship.

This time, Huiju came to Shanghai for the fourth time and his reputation soared. "Dapao Three Days," a completely new play, was paired with Jupeng's beautiful voice, which made it even more captivating. It shook the city for a time and everyone went to see it. On Saturday evening, the colleagues of Mingxing invited Xun Yan and his friend to a banquet at the company in Dumei Road. That night, it was drizzling and the road was muddy. Huiju and his friends, Furong Cao and Sha Youtian, arrived by car first and chatted with each other. Huiju was originally a consultant for the company and had often visited Shanghai before. Now, I feel that Huiju's appearance is more mature and his spirit is even more radiant. I asked Mr. Ishikawa and learned that he was directing "Such a Paradise" at the Second Photography Studio, so I went to visit in the rain. They were filming a scene in a dancer's rest room. Xia Peizhen, who played a famous dancer, was reclining on a sofa, holding her jade legs, with an unhappy expression on her face. She frequently called out with her fragrant mouth, laboriously massaging her swollen red legs, as if she would not be able to support herself if she had to dance again for a moment. Another dancer approached to offer her diligence, applying powder and massaging her, showing admiration that she could not have. Huiju saw this and smiled, and also asked Director Zhang about various techniques in cinematography. Huiju also pays close attention to the art of the silver screen. Soon, he returned to the opera troupe. Jupeng brought his young son and Yifen and others also came. They took their seats. There were three tables, and Detian, Lü Gong, and She Yu were all present. During the meal, Jianyun and Zhengqiu discussed improving the lyrics of Peking opera with Xun Yan and made many contributions. Jianyun also said that he was going to Hong Kong that day and would be back in about ten days, and he was deeply saddened that he could not listen to the opera every day. At that time, the sound of rain was getting louder outside the window and the clock had struck four. The hosts and guests then parted happily.

In Memory of My Uncle Yang Qiqing 121

— Di Xiangzhai Owner

Respectful and self-disciplined, benevolent and kind in dealing with people, he served as an official for decades, yet only his calligraphy and paintings remain. He retired early from many official affairs.

His teaching was like that of a teacher, his affection like that of a father. It has only been two months since we parted, and now his image and voice are no longer to be seen. Spring has ended in Jiangnan, and I am filled with sorrow.

A Strange Cure for Malaria 122

A strange method for treating malaria: Use a strip of white paper to write "two black plums, two red dates, two broad beans" according to the person's age, writing one bean for each year of age, ten beans for ten years old, twenty beans for twenty years old, and so on. After writing, fold the paper and tie it to the middle of the wrist or elbow one hour before the onset of malaria. When tying it, do not tell anyone. It must be divided into male left and female right, and then the malaria will not occur. This method is often very effective. Some people do not get better the first time, but get better the second time. It is indeed an extremely magical feat to cure diseases by writing the names of medicines and hanging them on the elbow without using any medicine. As summer gradually turns to autumn, there are those who suffer from this disease. Why not try it? (Know)

Around the Yellow Sea (22) 124

— Huang Yanpei

On the 19th, I arrived in Xijing. Visiting Japan, according to my opinion, it is better to say that Xijing is better than Tokyo.

That day, I visited Yasaka Shrine, Maruyama Park, the museum, the botanical garden, and the zoo, which had rare animals such as hippos and sea dogs. But the most adorable was Kinkaku-ji Temple.

The temple itself is nothing special, but the environment of the temple is extremely beautiful. After fourteen years, the long-awaited reunion made me linger reluctantly.

Revisiting Kinkaku-ji Temple

Having lived in Kinkaku-ji for ten years, my travels are somewhat traceable. Beyond the stream is a pavilion, beyond the pavilion is a road. The setting sun is silent, and the four mountains are deep. The dense pine shadows rise like a curtain, and ten thousand waves of damp green lock in the forest of illusion. The scenery of the stream and mountains is truly beautiful, but none of it is mine. Let my heart be at ease, and heaven enters the solitude.

On the 21st, I arrived in Kobe. How can I not recall my first trip abroad twenty-eight years ago when I arrived in Kobe? How can I not remember the righteousness and hospitality of my fellow villager, Mr. Chen Pingzhai, at that time? Our fellow villagers are truly good people. There was Mr. Chen abroad, and Mr. Yang at home. Alas, our fellow villagers!

Gu Junbingqi, Zhang Junbochu, and I, who went abroad at that time, are still alive today, while the Dongying Pavilion at No. 2 Fushan-cho, Maruyama, Hong District, Tokyo, no longer exists. Mr. Chen and Mr. Yang can no longer be seen. I revisited Mr. Chen's former residence on Shimonosho-dori, Kobe, and it has been transformed into a large building. After all, what have I done in these twenty-eight years of extended life? I must ask myself.

Twenty-eight years ago, I fled the country and Mr. Chen Pingzhai took me in here in Kobe. I am moved by my return.

Having lived, I am only like a mayfly. Twenty-eight years ago, I was left with nine deaths. Where else can I find the hundred-foot tower? My return only sees the waterfall flowing in pairs. One heart for a peaceful people. Green dragons fight fiercely in the four seas of autumn. Five voyages to Penglai are made day and night. How many splendid houses and how many mountain hills.

Casual Talks on the Lake (2) 125

— Tian Xu Wosheng

Vinegar fish cake is a famous delicacy of West Lake. It is said that Song Sao fish soup was once praised by Emperor Shou. In fact, fish soup is not vinegar fish. Hangzhou people make fish soup by steaming mandarin fish until cooked, removing the bones, and taking the meat to make soup. They add salt, egg yolk, and vinegar to make a hot and sour soup, which tastes rich and delicious, very similar to crab soup, so it is called fake crab soup. It is most fresh in February, which is when the so-called peach blossom flows and mandarin fish are fat. At that time, crucian carp have spawned and are thin, and Yangtze River Shad has not yet appeared, so only this fish is the best. However, the "West Lake Tour Record" says that there are many miscellaneous fish in the lake, but no mandarin fish. Therefore, Song Sao fish soup was uniquely praised by the emperor precisely because mandarin fish are not found in the lake. Vinegar fish is made by steaming kūn fish on water vapor and pouring vinegar sauce on it. The shredded scallions and shredded meat are not cooked in a pot, so they are fresh and tender. Kūn fish is the fish called kūn in Zhuangzi's "Northern Darkness," with an extremely large body and tender meat that is not old. It looks like a bluefish, but its body is long and round. In recent years, only small ones can be found on the market, called arrow-stem fish because they are thin, round, and slender, quite like arrow stems. Many restaurants on the lake cover them with bamboo cages and sink them in the water, calling them fish tanks. If a guest orders vinegar fish, it always comes with a cake. The so-called cake is made by slicing raw fish into extremely thin slices and mixing them with sesame oil, Sichuan peppercorns, and pepper powder, which tastes extremely fresh. Only those with no bones are considered skilled. This cannot be done in a home kitchen. Its shape is like a thin cake stuck on a Chen platter, so it is called a cake. It must be said that vinegar fish comes with a cake because a fish is specially killed just for this. Only the middle section has few bones and can be used for vinegar-braised fish. The market calls the middle section of vinegar fish the "middle section." If it does not come with a cake, then the fish is only cut in half, removing the head, to provide the tail meat, which has many thorns and cannot be eaten. Therefore, it must come with a cake so that the tail is useful and can be sliced into fish sashimi. Some people only like the cake, so they order a plate of fish sashimi. In the past, fish sashimi cost eight cents of silver per plate, the middle section of vinegar fish cost one dollar and six cents, and the whole vinegar fish cost two dollars and four cents. Whole fish refers to the whole fish with the head and tail attached. It is not half a fan. Hangzhou people do not eat this. If they do eat this, they are called "foreign plates." Hangzhou customs consider "foreign plates" and "large bowls" to be metaphors for largeness. In fact, there are only "large bowls" and no "foreign plates." The explanation of "foreign plates" has a different origin. In the past, the price of goods was calculated in silver, with seventy copper coins considered one cent of silver. Outsiders did not know the Hangzhou custom of considering one Mexican silver dollar worth seven dollars and two cents of treasury silver. In fact, seven dollars and two cents only required 504 copper coins. Copper coins were commonly called square boards. The market called them official coins. Each one weighed one mace according to the scale of the provincial treasury. Every tael of treasury silver exchanged for one thousand coins. Miscellaneous broken silver was taken to the treasury for exchange because its delivery to the Ministry of Revenue required it to be melted and made into ingots, each weighing fifty taels as standard. Therefore, a loss of about three-tenths was required. Only coins that were round and of the same size on both sides were exempt from loss in retail transactions. Because official coins were taken from the people and distributed to the people, and were not delivered to the Ministry of Revenue, the market considered seventy coins to be one cent of silver. One hundred coins would have been required to be one cent of silver, but the officials knew to use them instead of silver, so they reduced it by three-tenths.

Gold and Financial Gold Prices Rise Again 126

Soaring Ten Taels Nine

Spot goods are said to be for export. The gold price has been trending upward for the past three days, but not without fluctuations, rising and falling by three or four taels at times. From morning to evening, it totaled eleven taels. Looking back, although the situation was chaotic, confidence remained firm. The silver market rose slightly and was not affected. Instead, the gold price rose sharply. However, the turnover of colleagues was irregular, so the market price hovered around eight hundred taels. When foreign exchange trended upward, it was only half a grade, indicating a bright release and a dark contraction. The afternoon market was particularly promising. A large trader actively purchased, and there was talk that a certain bank wanted to ship spot goods for export. Under the influence of market rumors, the market became sharp. In the end, it reached 807-808 taels. However, since the foreign exchange market lacked activity on Wednesday, the silver market may decline this morning.

The previous market fluctuated several times. The July opening price in the morning rose by one tael to 796.5 taels. The big bars only rose by one-eighth. The silver price was the same. The private telegram slightly increased by sixteen points at a time to 96.23 taels. The buying sentiment in the market was strong. Sen Chang, Yong Shun, Li Yuanmao, Yong Da Xing, Yong Tong, and Tai Chang were all involved. Then it rose to 800 taels and eight cents. The exchange rate was still firm. Mitsui bought Dalian at 1.7125 taels. HSBC bought British gold at 121.875 to 125. Later, Yuancheng, Yongyuanmao, Yongyu Da, Yongfeng, and others sold out. And Mitsui sold British gold at 1875 to 25. When the pre-order was announced, it retreated to 97 taels. Since the price was extended by 125, US gold by 25, and Japanese gold by a decrease of 1.75, the internal market was stable and bought by Hongli, Qianchang, and Xiang. Therefore, it rose to 99 taels in a moment. Later, Yuhe, Qianchang, Xiang, Yongfeng, and Dadecheng sold out. At 9:50 AM, it was 95.5 taels and immediately rose again. Yuancheng, Yongtianxiang, Bingxing, Xinheng, and Qianchangxiang followed suit, adding more than four taels. There was a single tael or two. At 10:30, it was 800 taels. First Batch of New Wheat Arrives in Shanghai 135

Nanjing Goods Open at 3.9 Qian

Standard Wheat Varies

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat market in the morning, market sentiment was extremely unstable, with both near and distant contracts showing declines of 4-5 points. Because new wheat was about to arrive on the market and the weather was good, according to industry observers, the wheat harvest this year east of Wuxi and in the Shanghai area was not very good. However, the areas above Zhenjiang and in northern Jiangsu had about 70-80% of a normal harvest. Therefore, based on factual analysis, the situation was no worse than in previous years. The change in market sentiment was due to this reason. However, after the opening in the afternoon, because some speculators wanted to make up for their positions, large bulls again engaged in raising prices, so the market rebounded strongly. It is observed that the market may have to temporarily fluctuate for a while. As a result, this month's contract was down slightly by 2 points, July's was down slightly by 1 point, August's was unchanged, September/October's were up slightly by 1 point, and November's was down slightly by 1 point, it is said.

The first batch of new wheat arrived in Shanghai, totaling 400 bags of Nanjing goods, shipped jointly by four merchants from Nanjing. The opening price was 3.9 qian, and Hua Feng purchased it.

Flour Market Trends Weak Again 136

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market trended weak again in all months. Because most of the domestic merchants, in view of the favorable weather and the arrival of the new wheat harvest, felt that things were going smoothly. It was heard that although Shanghai had been experiencing a lot of rain the week before, northern Jiangsu had been drier. In recent days, samples of new wheat from various producing areas had been continuously sent to Shanghai, and the quality was very good, not as bad as expected. Therefore, not only had market sentiment in outside areas softened, but also speculative bulls in Shanghai had shifted from long to short positions. As a result, market sentiment was weak, and prices fell. June and July contracts were down about 2-1.5 points, and distant contracts were down about 1 point. By the afternoon closing, the market was initially weak but then rebounded strongly due to a surge in short covering and actual sales, recovering about 1 point from the morning. As a result, this month's contract was unchanged, July's was down by 2.5 li, August's was down by 5 li, September's was unchanged, and October and November's were up by 2.5 li, it is said.
