Public Bus Workers' Salary Increase 184

Company Submits Request to Public Utilities Bureau for Instructions

Details the Difficulties of Not Being Able to Raise Salaries

The workers of the Zhabei Chinese Merchants' Public Bus Company previously requested double pay on racing days, which the company refused. Subsequently, the labor union sent letters to various agencies and the company, detailing the reasons for requesting a salary increase and attaching five questions: (1) Regarding the withholding of union dues; (2) Regarding the tire case of driver Zhu Tian; (3) Regarding the demerit of driver Wu Pingji; (4) Regarding the demerit for driver assaulting another person; (5) Regarding Zhu Ahe's bonus. The text was several thousand words long and provided sufficient justification. Yesterday, the company submitted a document to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to be forwarded to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau for instructions regarding this matter. Each of the above five points was debated in detail, and a detailed response was given to the workers' request for double pay on racing days, as follows (abridged): Regarding double pay on racing days, although there are many passengers on racing days, it is not a regular occurrence. It is unreasonable to demand double pay. The company's daily income is insufficient to cover expenses. The loss of 20,000 yuan last year is known to the authorities and understood by us. Although business revenue is one to two hundred dollars higher than usual on racing days, this cannot compensate for losses due to rainy weather. During the rainy season in spring, the roads are muddy, and daily losses are no less than two to three hundred dollars. With the school holidays approaching in the summer, the company relies heavily on students for business. During July and August, the daily loss due to the lack of students is at least about two hundred yuan. Furthermore, the cost of gasoline, tires, and machinery are all purchased from abroad, which has been greatly affected by the rising price of gold. In this situation, it is difficult to continue operations. The labor union is ungrateful and often makes unreasonable and embarrassing demands. The company is suffering and has nowhere to complain. Therefore, we have prepared a detailed report and ask that it be forwarded to the Municipal Social Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters for instructions.

Salvaging the Sunken Dachang Steamer at the Wusong Mouth 185

Work Commenced Yesterday

Four Months of Construction Required

The Dachang steamer, which was sunk at the Wusong Mouth after a collision, is obstructing traffic on a major waterway. The Customs Service has decided to salvage the ship to facilitate navigation. The salvage operation has been contracted to the Japanese-owned Katsumura & Co., located at 188 Minhang Road in Shanghai, and officially began yesterday. A temporary office has been built on the coast of Paotaiwan. The director of the Seventh District of Public Security, Zhao, has dispatched several police officers to provide security. Salvaging operations are scheduled from 10:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m. daily and are expected to take about four months to complete. The salvage cost is estimated at 180,000 yuan. It is reported that most of the ship will need to be destroyed with explosives, and a temporary notice will be issued to incoming and outgoing vessels to avoid the area.

Rickshaw Dispute in Western Shanghai 186

In the area of Caojiadu, Western Shanghai, near Songqiao and Xinjing, which lies on the boundary between the Chinese and foreign concessions, most of the roads are built by the foreign concession. There are over four hundred rickshaws, all of which are owner-operated and therefore unlicensed. Recently, the Municipal Government has recovered police powers, and the number of rickshaws in the northern and southern parts of the city has increased from 7,400 to 10,000. Last August, the rickshaw drivers in western Shanghai petitioned the Municipal Government for reorganization, but this increase of 2,600 rickshaws has only allocated to Pudong, Wusong, and the northern and southern parts of the city, and the vehicles in western Shanghai were not included in the reorganization. The Municipal Council has also complained about the unlicensed vehicles in that area, causing great panic among the more than two thousand rickshaw pullers in western Shanghai. On the other day, over three hundred of them went to the Municipal Government to petition and elected Peng Yuzhi, Wang Chenglian, Li Zhiliang, and Yu Hainan as representatives to present their petition. An official from the Second Division of the Municipal Government received them and instructed the representatives to lead the people back and await the Municipal Government's reply. Yesterday, the Sixth Precinct Police Station confiscated all unlicensed vehicles. At approximately 9:00 a.m., eight vehicles were confiscated at the north end of Zhongshan Bridge and transported to the Municipal Council by truck. This action agitated all two hundred rickshaw pullers, who blocked the truck and prevented it from leaving. After persuasion by the director of the Sixth Precinct, Ren Luping, to avoid violence and await the Municipal Government's reply, the crowd dispersed.

Major Theft at British Woman's Home Solved 187

The case of the theft of jewelry worth 15,000 yuan and bank certificates worth 5,000 yuan from the home of British woman Mrs. Magulf on the night of the 25th of last month has been solved by the French Police yesterday. They apprehended a thief who was attempting to sell some of the stolen goods. Because he was caught with the stolen goods, he was arrested. Another person was detained, but this person worked as a dancer and could prove that he was elsewhere when the theft occurred, so he was soon released. It is reported that both men were Caucasians.

Quan Zhaoxin's Wife Returns to Ningbo and Does Not Return 188

Quan Zhaoxin, a native of this county, lives in the Shuanggang area north of the Hu Jia Mu Bridge in Hongkou. He is a coppersmith by trade and is currently twenty-one years old. He married Chen Zhou's daughter, Jin Lang, a woman from Meijia Lane near Beishuanggang, through a matchmaker when he was eighteen years old. Jin Lang is twenty-three years old this year. The following year, she gave birth to a son, who died at three months old. In the early days of Jin Lang's marriage, the relationship with her husband was considered harmonious, but recently, she suddenly changed her behavior and frequently returned to Ningbo on various pretexts. This time, on the 4th day of last month (May) (i.e., March 17th of the lunar calendar), she left at approximately 7:00 a.m. on the pretext of returning to Ningbo and has not returned despite repeated attempts to contact her. Quan Zhaoxin, therefore, was anxious and filed a lawsuit with the Mediation Department of the local court to demand the return of his wife, stating that his wife's mother, Chen Zhou, was hiding his daughter and refused to return her. He requested that she be summoned to court and ordered to return his wife, Jin Lang, to him so that they could be reunited. Yesterday, presiding judge Chen Bingxin opened the court and summoned both parties for mediation. Quan Zhaoxin testified to the previous events and stated that he was still able to see Jin Lang at her mother's house when he went to pick her up the first time, but she had not been seen on the second attempt. His mother-in-law only stated that she would send her daughter back after a few days of lingering, but this was repeatedly delayed, and he was never able to see her despite repeated attempts to pick her up. Therefore, he had no choice but to file a lawsuit to demand her return. The opposing party, Chen Zhou, 62 years old, testified that Jin Lang was her daughter and that her daughter had left her husband's home and that she was not responsible. The judge said, "In the end, she is still your daughter. I will give you one month to find and return her, while Quan Zhaoxin will assist in the search." Chen replied, "I have nowhere to search." The judge, finding that mediation had failed, instructed Quan Zhaoxin to file a formal lawsuit separately.

A Son-in-Law Is Rejected and Sues 189

Wang Qiutang, a farmer from Chen Village Township, Sanlintang, Pudong, has no sons, only one daughter named Wang Siying, who is 21 years old this year. On February 25th, the 17th year of the Republic of China, he hired Wang Gen'nan through a matchmaker to be his son-in-law. Gen'nan was renamed Junqi and lived peacefully at his home. However, on the 12th day of the first lunar month of last year, Gen'nan's biological father (who lived in Beicai, Pudong) became seriously ill, so he rushed back to his home in Beicai to care for him. After his father recovered, he returned to Wang's house, but was unexpectedly rejected. Feeling aggrieved, he hired Lawyer Yao Wenshou to sue Wang Qiutang in the Mediation Court of the District Court, accusing him of going back on his marriage agreement and requesting that the marriage be maintained. As mediation failed, he formally filed a lawsuit. The defendant, Wang Qiutang, also hired Lawyer Li Yuan to present his defense. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Zhenhai opened the court to hear the case. The plaintiff, Wang Gen'nan, was absent. His representative, Lawyer Yao Wenshou, appeared in court and stated the plaintiff's age and background. He said that the plaintiff, Wang Gen'nan, was 25 years old and a local. The defendant, Wang Qiutang, stated that he was 51 years old, lived in Sanlin Township, and made a living by farming. Wang Siying testified that she was 21 years old and did not want to marry him (the plaintiff) because he was gluttonous and lazy. Judge Zhao said that since the plaintiff was absent today, no debate would be held, and instructed the lawyers of both parties to go out and reconcile. He also scheduled another hearing.

Wang Songbai Sells His Wife 190

Wang Chenshi Does Not Eat for Three Days

Grandma Sun Demonstrates Admirable Chivalry

Wang Chenshi, a woman from Changzhou, married Wang Songbai at the age of 17. Songbai, however, did not engage in proper employment and found it difficult to make a living. He instructed his wife to work as a female worker in the Gongda Cotton Mill in Shanghai West. All the hard-earned income was spent by Songbai. Recently, Songbai had a wild idea and gave his wife's birth certificate to street rascals, Electric Car Monk, Wang Jiali A'hu, Yu Futao, and others, putting into practice the principle of selling his wife. He had previously booked a room in the Southeast Hotel, planning to trick Wang Chenshi into going to the hotel to be sold for 500 yuan. At the time, these people did not have a single penny on them and took the five yuan that Wang Chenshi had in her pocket. The next day, they changed to the Wujiang Hotel on Sima Road and held her there for three days, denying her food for three days. At this time, Grandma Sun, Wang Chenshi's second landlord, heard about the matter. On May 10th, she went to the hotel to persuade them, but everyone refused.

They Demanded 90 Yuan to Cover the Losses of the Street Rascals for Selling the Body. Grandma Sun, filled with righteous indignation, volunteered to stay at the hotel in place of Wang Chenshi to raise the money. After Wang Chenshi left, she felt unwilling to accept this fate and hired a lawyer to report the matter to the Sima Road Police Station. The police station, together with the Lao Zhou Police Station, went to the Wujiang Hotel and arrested all those involved. After questioning them, they instructed the three parties to file a lawsuit in the Special District Court. Yesterday was the date for the trial, but the defendants failed to appear. The court ordered warrants to be issued for their arrest for a retrial.

Another Accomplice, Zhou Weiming, Is Arrested in the Li Zuoming Embezzlement Case 195

A 16-Year-Old Apprentice

Li Zuoming, a postal worker from Ningbo, was suspended by the post office and, unable to make a living, began collecting packages from shops under the pretext of sending them by mail, forging customs tax receipts and embezzling taxes and postage. After the post office learned of this, they reported it to the police, who arrested Li and his accomplices, Xu Linxiang and Shui Quanxiang, and seized counterfeit seals and receipts. They were sent to the Special District Court for investigation, as reported earlier. Recently, the Chinese and Western detectives handling the case found that Yuxin Stationery Company at No. 133 Jiaotong Road had also used Li to send goods on five occasions, and the five customs tax receipts held were all forged. The money was divided between Li and Zhou Weiming, a 16-year-old apprentice from Qingpu at Yuxin Company. Zhou was arrested and sent to the Special Court for questioning yesterday morning. Zhou confessed that all the goods sent by mail from the company were brought to Li's place by him, and the fees given totaled more than 60 yuan. Li received 20% and he received 80%. Judge Xiao approved the request of the police lawyer, Li Zhishan, and ordered Zhou to be detained for a joint trial with Li Zuoming at a later date.

The Uselessness of Play 197

Qi A'si Loses Her Life

Xiao Wanzi Denies Injury

Qi Chen, a woman from Yancheng, whose daughter Qi A'si, 19, was on a boat in the river at Pingyin Bridge, Rihui Port. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, she was washing coal dregs by the river and got into a fight with Cao Xiao Wanzi, the son of Cao Lu, a woman, over teasing. A Record of the Hubei Fellow Villagers' Joyful Banquet 198

The Hubei Association in Shanghai held a public banquet at the Atlantic Western Restaurant the night before, in honor of the former Hubei Chairman Fang Muren, Xia Douyin, Commander of the Military, and Cai Fuqing, a philanthropist from Hankou, as well as representatives attending the National Assembly. More than 100 people from the political, commercial, industrial, academic, and journalistic circles in Shanghai attended. Gao Jianqing was elected to give a speech, in which he briefly stated that when Chairman Fang was in charge of Hubei's administration, his political reputation was outstanding and obvious to all. He supervised and suppressed the bandits and had almost eliminated them, but his efforts were abandoned when he left for other duties for the country. His colleagues still feel sorry for this. This time, as a representative of Hubei merchants, he attended the National Assembly and suggested revitalizing industry and commerce to open up sources of profit for the country. His vision is admirable to his colleagues. Commander Xia has always been dedicated to suppressing bandits and pacifying the people, and his reputation has spread everywhere he has been. This time, he was appointed as the garrison commander and has fulfilled his duties to the utmost, relying on local stability and tranquility. All Hubei people deeply admire him. However, at present, there are still bandits who have not been completely suppressed, and there are many brigands who want to cut off their roots, relying on security. If the soldiers leave, the bandits will come, which is not without worry. Before the bandits in Hubei Province are completely suppressed, we hope that the authorities will transfer the troops in all defense areas of the province to the authorities so that they will not be transferred to other places, so as to ensure the safety and security of the people. This is what the colleagues earnestly pray for. The representatives attending the meeting have been running around for the country and working hard. Mr. Fuqing and Mr. Sheng Bochang came to Shanghai to participate in the peace prayer, hoping to avoid the catastrophe. This shows their compassion. Although Mr. Liao is old, he still repeatedly supports the Hubei Association in Shanghai. The gentlemen have either contributed to the party and the country or benefited their hometown. This time, they are resting in Shanghai during their public duties. The colleagues have prepared a humble meal to express their admiration. Mr. Fang Benren replied that he was temporarily in charge of Hubei's administration and that his affairs were contrary to his wishes and that he had no achievements. Later, he left Hubei due to an incident, which led to the abandonment of his responsibilities. He was ashamed that Mr. Gao Jianqing, on behalf of you gentlemen, had generously praised him. Fortunately, Commander Xia is guarding Wuhan and its surrounding areas, and the bandits in Hubei Province will not spread. This time, he and Commander Xia returned to Hubei and decided to report to the authorities on their behalf. There will be very good measures to be taken to eliminate them as soon as possible to comfort the elders. The evening ended at 8 o'clock, and everyone dispersed in joy.

A Lost Girl Awaits Collection 200

A girl, Wu Jinmei, 9 years old, from Suzhou, wearing a red striped cloth shirt and trousers, got lost in the French Concession on June 1. The police found her and brought her to the police station. When asked about her address, she was vague and unable to answer. The police chief ordered her to be temporarily taken care of while waiting for her family to claim her.

Fire on Guangzhao Road 201

Behind a rickshaw company on Guangzhao Road, Zhabei, there is an open space of about one mu, filled with thatched huts occupied by no less than fifty households. Yesterday afternoon at around 5 p.m., a fire suddenly broke out in one of the thatched huts due to unknown reasons. The fire spread quickly, and more than 20 thatched huts were completely destroyed. Fortunately, firefighters from various fire brigades rushed to the scene and fought bravely to extinguish the fire, preventing it from spreading further. When the fire broke out, most of the residents there were working outside, and because the thatched huts were easily flammable, it was not known who was responsible for starting the fire. However, according to the victims, the fire started in Zhao Lipei's house. Zhao was a worker at the Fuxin Flour Mill and was not at home when the accident occurred. His son, Wenliang, 18, was detained by the Fourth District Police Station for questioning.

"Springtime Dance Hall" Premieres in Beijing 202

Ms. Fannie Brice, an American comedian and dancer, is a mainstay of the renowned Ziegfeld Follies and the Balas Ballet in Europe and America. Her pearl-like voice and exquisite dance moves, combined with humorous actions, are especially captivating. Ms. Brice recently starred in the full-length musical sound film "Springtime Dance Hall" with Charlie Chaplin, Fan Benke, and Bickford, under the United Artists Film Company. The clear songs and wonderful dances, the pearl-like laughter and jade-like fragrance, are like placing the audience in front of the stage. It is said that the film will be screened at the Beijing Grand Theatre for three consecutive days starting today, which will be a great pleasure for the senses.

Wang Yuandao Guoyao, located at Nan Zhujia Bridge in the French Concession, officially opened yesterday. The business part of the store is divided into five departments: sliced medicinal herbs, pills and powders, ginseng and bird's nest, prescription reception and medicine delivery, and medicine decoction service. All businesses are very developed. The prescription reception and medicine delivery department provides fast delivery without charging delivery fees. The medicine decoction service employs experienced medicine decoctionists who specialize in medicine decoction and maintain the effective ingredients within a standard time through strict calibration, ensuring no errors. General customers enjoy its convenience and reliability. Yesterday, there were dozens of phone calls for prescription decoction. In addition, the store's invented Qiang Shen Bu Lao Dan (Strength-Enhancing and Anti-Aging Pill), Huatan Cough Ling (Phlegm-Resolving Cough Remedy), and Wang Dao Anti-Epidemic Water are also sold in large quantities. It is estimated that the total business yesterday was more than 20,000 yuan.

The Shanghai Zhabei District Fourth Fire Brigade, located at the corner of Qingyun Road and Baoxing Road in Zhabei, was initiated last autumn by local gentry and merchants Chen Yousheng, Yang Caiqing, and others at the request of shops and residents along Baoshan Road, Baoxing Road, and Qingyun Road. After being approved by the Municipal Government Public Security Bureau, it proceeded with the establishment of the association, such as setting up a clubhouse, purchasing pump trucks, belts, and other fire-fighting equipment, operating diligently and painstakingly. It is heard that it has been approved by the Municipal Government to handle it. In recent days, donation booklets have been distributed by board members and members to enthusiastic local people and factories to encourage donations, regardless of the amount, as a voluntary contribution. Merchants and residents there, in view of the importance of fire prevention, are happy to donate, so the number of people who pledge to donate is extremely enthusiastic. It is also heard that the association is now fully equipped and is scheduled to hold a formal inauguration ceremony at 9 a.m. on June 7. Letters have been sent to various agencies and organizations to send personnel to guide them. The association staff has been working quite busily in recent days.

Letter Requesting the Construction of the Northern Section of Tongzhou Road 206

A letter from the Real Estate Department of the Kenye Bank to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association states: "We are writing to inform you that the northern section of Tongzhou Road, Tonghaili, in the Eastern District, which is leased by our department, is rugged and difficult to walk on, and the accumulation of filth hinders sanitation. Several years ago, Yiyuan Company sent a letter to the Engineering Bureau requesting construction, but it was not approved. At that time, there were relatively few residents along the road, and the amount of donations that could be collected was not large, so it was understandable that this was not paid attention to. Now the situation is very different, and the annual income from house rent is already quite considerable. If construction is not carried out for a long time, how can the residents be comforted and the pedestrians benefited? Furthermore, residents there have complained one after another to the lessees of our department, and even threatened to withhold rent as a protest. In this situation, the rent of our department's houses has been greatly affected. Furthermore, we have sent a letter to the Engineering Bureau requesting early construction, but we have not received a reply. We have always admired your association's representation of the people, and we dare to prepare a letter requesting that you forward a letter to the Engineering Bureau to expedite the construction of the northern section of Tongzhou Road. We respectfully wish you all the best. Real Estate Department of the Chinese Kenye Bank, June 2."

Art World

Concerning National Culture 210

— One Remark

Recently, while reading Hu Yuzhi's Impressions of Moscow (9) in a certain publication, the section on national culture and international culture contained many pertinent points. I have transcribed and supplemented it as follows:

Impressions of Moscow (9) Yu Zhi 211

National Culture and International Culture

I had a casual conversation with Comrade U regarding literature and art, which yielded some new insights.

This is a major paradox: Bolsheviks are thoroughgoing internationalists in their political stance, yet they are also thoroughgoing nationalists in their cultural and artistic stance.

I believe that no government in the world promotes and protects national culture, national languages, and national arts as much as the Soviet government. (Of course, the national culture, national languages, and national arts I am referring to here are not specifically Russian culture, language, and arts. The Soviet Union encompasses dozens of different nationalities, and the Belarussian nationality is only one of them. Treating Soviet nationalism and Russian nationalism as the same thing is the most common, easily made, and most important mistake.) Before the revolution, people within the territory of the Tsar generally only knew of a Russian Empire and a Russian nationality. Only after the October Revolution were other nationalities discovered besides the Russian nationality, such as Ukrainian, Belarusian, Cossack, Georgian, Tatar, Armenian, Tadjiks, Khiegizes, Uzdeks, Tuscimans, Tadshiks, Klimea, Balhkiriens, Jakutions, Komis, Kauakopaken, and countless other strange nationalities that are difficult to enumerate and pronounce. Not only was this large group of nationalities discovered, but also the unique cultures, languages, and literatures of these nationalities. Within the Soviet Union, all languages have the same legal effect as Russian. The station names marked at the many stations I passed through were listed in four, five, seven, or eight languages. The postage stamps, postal postcards, and banknotes issued by the state are printed with various strange characters. The state printing office uses seventy or eighty languages to print textbooks, magazines, newspapers, and literary works, some of which had never been printed on paper during the Tsarist era.

The same is true in literature and art. Russian literature from the latter half of the nineteenth century to the beginning of the twentieth century, such as the works of Turgenev and Chekhov, was greatly influenced by Western European literature in terms of technique and thought, so it was universal. On the contrary, the newly emerging proletarian literature is local, rustic, and intensely nationalistic. The emerging music and dance arts are also filled with the sentiments of various folk songs and folk dances. The greatest source of proletarian literature and art is folk literature and art, so it cannot but be nationalistic.

Take Comrade U as an example. He comes from a proletarian background in the city and embraced Bolshevism at an early age, joining the Red Army. Almost all of the novels he writes use the Red-White War as their subject matter, but he writes them entirely in Tatar, not in Russian. Although he can also write in Russian and his Russian works would reach a larger audience than his Tatar works, he feels that only by using his native language can he faithfully express his feelings. According to Comrade U, in the Soviet Union, those who stand at the forefront of the revolution in politics, society, and thought are the most insistent on protecting national culture and language. For example, the Soviet government has recently advocated changing all the languages used within the Soviet Union to Latin alphabet spelling, but this proposal has not yet been implemented, solely because several important political leaders firmly oppose it. The reason for their opposition is the fear that the form of the language will lose its special national character after adopting the Latin alphabet.

This seems theoretically inconsistent. The Bolsheviks, on the one hand, proclaim that proletarians have no fatherland, and on the other hand, they strive to promote and protect national culture. The issue of national culture sparked fierce debates among party theorists several years ago, especially among those in the Commissariat of Education (冀), who strongly opposed promoting national culture. But finally, Stalin's position prevailed. Stalin argued that the ultimate goal of the revolution is to create a world culture to replace all national cultures, but the emergence of world culture must occur many years after the success of the world revolution. In the current transitional stage, the proletarian regime is limited to the borders of the Soviet Union, so creating a world culture is obviously impossible. Moreover, the creation of world culture must occur after all nations have the equal freedom to develop their national characteristics and national cultures. Many of the world's small nationalities are still under imperialist oppression and cannot uniquely develop their national cultures, so the first step must be to liberate and develop national cultures, and only then can world culture emerge. Otherwise, suppressing the growth and development of the cultures and languages of various small nationalities within the Soviet Union would only create the superior position of Russian national culture and language, using Russian culture to unify other national cultures, which would be no different from the assimilation policies of imperialism. Therefore, at this time, we should strive to support the development of the cultures, languages, and arts of various small nationalities. Even after the political and national boundaries are eliminated, national culture will still need to be cultivated and supported for a considerable period of time, because the more fully national culture develops, the richer the quality of world culture will be in the future. Therefore, in terms of cultural vision, Bolsheviks should be nationalistic and liberal.

What I would like to add is that:

Our country's literature and art have been in turmoil since the May Fourth Movement. It was not until June 1, 1930 (民國十九年) that there was an accurate expression of how our country's literature and art should develop in the future. On that day, we had the Declaration of the Nationalistic Literary Movement. Since the publication of that declaration, its influence has certainly been profound, but it must be said that very few people truly understand national literature, national art, and nationalistic literature and art. A year later, Mr. Yuzhi returned from his travels in Europe. This article on national culture and international culture can be said to be an expression of deep sympathy from him and his group for the movement we are advocating. Therefore, it is evident that we should be engaged in the efforts of nationalistic literature and art, and the lasting greatness of nationalistic literature and art.

In our country, the literature on national literature and art must include (1) "Three Words on Art" by Fu Yanchang and Zhu Yingpeng, Fu Yanchang's "Miscellaneous Leaves of the Sixteenth Year", Ye Qiuyuan's "The Nationality and Internationality of Art" and "Collected Essays on Nationalistic Literature and Art", etc. Fu Yanchang can be said to be the pioneer of promoting national literature and national art in our country.

Literary Anecdotes

The Final Moments of Two Poets 212

— Cai

— Byron and Shelley

Byron had a very passionate sympathy for the Greeks who were resisting Turkish tyranny and seeking independence. Therefore, in July 1823, he boarded the Hercules and set off for the East to actually participate in the Greek army and provide some assistance.

Accompanying him were Count Gamba and Trelawny, as well as the Italian physician, Dr. Francesco. The ship carried two cannons, five horses, a quantity of ammunition, and 50,000 Spanish gold coins, all to help the war of independence.

Byron's heart was truly burning with love for Greece. They arrived in Missolonghi in January of the following year, where the inhabitants greeted them with cheers. The army fired a salute, and Governor-General Mavrocordatos came out to welcome them in person. Byron, dressed in a red military uniform, looked like a world-class hero being celebrated by everyone. After joining the army, Byron was no longer a poet wielding a pen but a general wielding a sword.

Later, he was appointed governor. When attacking Lepanto, his commanding presence was awe-inspiring. Who would have known that he was a poet who should have been refined and gentle? At that time, his passion was also ignited by the bravery of the Greek army defending their homeland, so he appeared even more magnificent and great.

At that time, it almost completely eliminated the sentimental, easily angered, and easily sighed poet of the past, and instead showed the demeanor of a respectable military commander with self-control.

In the past, Byron was willing to use his own money to help any friend, and now he was also willing to provide his income to the Greek army. Therefore, the Greeks admired and loved him even more. Everyone understood that he was indeed sincerely helping Greece's independence.

One day, when the military operations were nearing their end, he and Gamba rode on horseback to the coast for a walk, and despite the rain, they went boating at sea. The following month, he also went for a walk in the woods in the rain.

In the end, his grand ambitions did not succeed, and at the same time, he was afflicted by illness, so he could no longer stand.

While he was groaning with fever, all the poets, including Dr. Francesco, took care of him day and night, silently praying for the feverish poet to recover. While feverish, he often shouted, "Forward, forward!" Later, he also said:

"Although I have sacrificed my time, health, and possessions, and now my body is in such a state, Greece, Greece, what will you ultimately achieve?"

These were his last words on April 19, 1824, as he was dying. He was only thirty-seven years old.

After the news of Byron's death spread, the entire Greek territory was completely enveloped in grief and sorrow. At that time, thirty-seven cannon shots, the same number as his age, were fired in mourning.

Six years after his death, Greece successfully achieved independence, finally fulfilling his last wish.

Later, to repay this meritorious figure who helped with independence, Greece built a statue of the heroic and talented poet holding his beloved dog in Hyde Park in England as a permanent memorial.

On July 8, 1822, Shelley returned from visiting his old friend Haydon and boarded the Don Juan, a boat he had built with Byron, from Spezia Bay. The pure white sails of the boat shining on the sea waves were even more beautiful than words could describe.

His friend Trelawny was on another boat and saw the Don Juan carrying Shelley, floating lightly on the sea waves.

It was a very hot and sultry day, so soon a big storm arose on the sea. The sound of the waves roared, the wind was very urgent, and a whirlpool formed. The Don Juan carrying Shelley disappeared in this storm.

Of course, Trelawny, on the deck where he had safely taken refuge, thought of his friend who had gone far away and did not know where he was going. He did not care that the waves were crashing at his feet and the rain had soaked his whole body. He could only shout:

"Shelley, what happened to Shelley!"

Although the storm stopped silently not long after, and Spezia Bay regained its original calm and beautiful southern sea color, the Don Juan was nowhere to be found.

Trelawny told the news to Hunt and Byron. Byron was so shocked that he could not speak, and his lips trembled with pallor.

Although the friends searched all over the coast, they could not find any wreckage of the Don Juan or Shelley's body. It was not until July 18 that Shelley's body was found on the coast of Viareggio. The body's coat still contained collections of poems by Aeschylus and Keats. The collection of Keats' poems was still open.

On August 6, Byron, Hunt, and Trelawny cremated Shelley's remains in mourning and sadness, and the ashes were buried in Rome.

He, like Byron, was called a genius poet of a generation. His life was seven years shorter than Byron's, and he was only thirty years old.

Manuscript Guidelines for the Art World 213

(1) Articles should be limited to news, commentary, and introductions regarding recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature both domestically and abroad.

(2) Photos should be limited to recent portraits of domestic and foreign artists and their works, as well as various photographs related to the above.

(3) The word count for each article should not exceed 2,000 words at most.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

Page 20

Social News

The Most Glorious Page of the Emden (Continued) 214

— Lin

Falling into the Water

Shells were still exploding everywhere. The vibration from our own cannons caused many people to fall into the water. I dragged a friend out of the water three times, but the fourth time he fell into the water and drowned before I could notice. I myself fell out of the ship and grabbed a rope from the mast to avoid falling into the water. But now the ship was sinking and I was almost meeting the water.

Later, I lost consciousness. I did not wake up until I was shaken by the sound of shelling. I was lying in front of the command tower. The Sydney came to attack again for half a day because we did not agree to surrender and continued to fire at our ship. I saw Captain von Müller order the survivors to hide behind the armored tower, but he himself stood in front, his tall figure clearly visible above the waterline, directly facing the Sydney's guns. I really did not understand that he was determined to share the fate of most of his men, but strangely, the flying shells killed and injured the people around him, but they did not touch him at all. Fate did not allow him to die with his men and ship.

Flames and Waves

By the next day, the waves were exceptionally turbulent and the situation on the ship was getting worse. The entire ship was still on fire. Huge seagulls were attacking us from time to time. There was no fresh water on the ship and the injured people were in terrible condition. Therefore, I decided to jump off the ship and transport the injured to the island. I was granted permission by Captain von Müller. I will especially never forget him looking at me, hoping that I would succeed.

Under the guidance of Colonel Weidtfeld, everything was handled very carefully. A long rope was tied around my waist and I was told to take it to the island. Holding a large knife in one hand to defend against the sharks, I jumped towards the crest of a giant wave. A vortex, its center below the bow of the ship, pulled me under the keel of the Emden. When the speed of the whirlpool decreased slightly, I saw that the whirlpool was at least ten feet in diameter. In addition, I saw the Emden sandwiched between two coral reefs, which extended from the shore like fingers. This, of course, was the reason for the giant whirlpool.

I was not alone. Opposite me, just like me, without help, there was a large shark rolled in the vortex, its white belly facing me. Then, for a moment, there was movement. The seawater slowly rose and filled the bottom of the vortex. I heard a loud cracking sound and the bottom of the vortex was filled with strange green light. The waves all converged into it. Suddenly, a force lifted the water from the vortex like a giant fountain, throwing me straight up. The keel of the Emden passed before my eyes like a red line. In that instant, I felt like I had lost weight. I saw the big shark go across the bow of the ship. Now I felt like there was a turning point.

When I regained consciousness for the first time, I found myself in turbulent waves, far away from the Emden and about two hundred yards from the beach. I swam towards the beach, but strangely, every time I swam, a giant wave came. I was not hit on the surface of the wave, but was hit on the bottom of the water. The rope around my body was wrapped around the reef. I was tethered like a buoy. Finally, the rope broke and I was driven by the waves without the power to resist. I tried several times without success and gave up.

I sank into the water two or three times, each time very safely. I saw the azure sky, the white sandy beach, and the palm trees on the shore gently swaying in the breeze. I felt incredibly happy in my heart. In an instant, I was lifted into the air again, riding the broken waves and thrown onto the beach. I regained my life.

Sometimes I dare not call this unexpected encounter fortunate. I just wanted to rest peacefully for a while, but God was playing tricks on me again. My explanation is this: like a rat submerged in water, I convulsed and stretched out my legs. My right foot touched a rock and was washed back into the water.

Iron Cross Award

For the above experience, I received the Iron Cross First Class. Later, many of my friends told me that at that time, they thought my life was not worth a penny on the deck. Later, my companions all gathered together and headed towards the beach using empty ammunition boxes. The condition of the injured was very miserable. People without arms or legs were rolled by the waves and lay on the beach. Those without help cried out for thirst, unable to get water. Finally, they drank a mouthful of seawater to quench their thirst like crazy. Even those of us who could walk could not think of a way to stop them from drinking seawater. Therefore, the ship's assistant medical officer actually drank seawater to quench his thirst and lost his life.

The second problem was transporting the injured, because it was very dangerous for us to be naked under the scorching sun. The few of us who were still able to move carried the injured to the shade of trees and rocks to rest.

Nearby was a coconut tree full of coconuts. We spent half an hour climbing up forty feet. Later, I finally reached the top of the tree and threw down fifty or sixty coconuts to the ground. Fortunately, I left four for myself, because my companions ate all the coconuts that were thrown down without thinking. I gave the few I had left to the weak and those who could not get to the bottom of the tree to eat together.

Thirsty Madness

Because I was unbearable with thirst, I started having hallucinations, showing a glass of beer, cool and delicious, with foam floating around the glass. But this elusive glass often evaded me. I chased desperately until I fell to the ground and lost consciousness. I also dreamed in my head that many companions were cursing at the water tanks on the ship.

When I woke up, I saw small bugs crawling on my skin, biting me very painfully, and long thorns being dragged out of my skin. A wild bird stopped beside us, using its sharp hooked beak to tear the muscles of the helpless injured. Both afraid and angry, I used my strength to kill dozens of them. From then on, we felt that there must be two guards to drive away the wild birds to prevent them from harming the injured.

I walked back and forth in the bushes, preparing to look for something to eat. Suddenly, I saw a large seabird about to lay eggs, all white, flying in the air with a wingspan of six feet long. It left a large egg on the white sand. I took the egg in my hand and the huge bird kept calling. Surprised, I put the egg back in its original place. I saw an extraordinary thing in nature. A small pointed beak broke out of the shell and divided the eggshell into two halves. There was a blue bird on the beach, calling to its mother miserably. I looked and thought, I am a city child and have never seen such a thing. The old bird hovering above my head flew down calmly in a moment and clamped the little bird, stretching out its wings to protect the little bird from the sunlight. Finally, she squatted on top of the nest, looking directly at me.
